<p>The <b>Chesapeake Bay</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/tʃ/: 'ch' in 'China'">tʃ</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i><b>CHESS</b>-ə-peek</i></small></a>) is an <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> in the U.S. states of <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, lying inland from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and surrounded to the west by the <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North American</a> mainland and to the east by the <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Peninsula" title="Delmarva Peninsula">Delmarva Peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT16_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT16-2">[2]</a></sup> It is the largest estuary in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> With its northern portion in Maryland and the southern part in Virginia, the Chesapeake Bay is a very important feature for the ecology and economy of those two states, as well as others. More than 150 major rivers and streams flow into the Bay's 64,299-square-mile (166,534 km<sup>2</sup>) <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drainage basin</a>, which covers parts of six states (<a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, Maryland, Virginia and <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>) and all of <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT16_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsT16-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fs102-98_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-fs102-98-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bay is approximately 200 miles (320 km) long from its northern headwaters in the <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_River" title="Susquehanna River">Susquehanna River</a> to its outlet in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. It is 2.8 miles (4.5 km) wide at its narrowest (between <a href="/wiki/Kent_County,_Maryland" title="Kent County, Maryland">Kent County's</a> Plum Point near Newtown and the <a href="/wiki/Harford_County,_Maryland" title="Harford County, Maryland">Harford County</a> shore near Romney Creek) and 30 miles (48 km) at its widest (just south of the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a>). Total shoreline including tributaries is 11,684 miles (18,804 km), circumnavigating a surface area of 4,479 square miles (11,601 km<sup>2</sup>). Average depth is 21 feet (6.4 m), reaching a maximum of 174 feet (53 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297bathysurveys_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-297bathysurveys-5">[5]</a></sup> The Bay is spanned twice, in Maryland by the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">Chesapeake Bay Bridge</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Point_State_Park" title="Sandy Point State Park">Sandy Point</a> (near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annapolis" title="Annapolis">Annapolis</a>) to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kent_Island,_Maryland" title="Kent Island, Maryland">Kent Island</a> and in Virginia by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge-Tunnel" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel">Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Charles,_Virginia" title="Cape Charles, Virginia">Cape Charles</a>. Known for both its beauty and bounty, the Bay has become "emptier", with fewer crabs, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oysters" title="Oysters">oysters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waterman_(occupation)" title="Waterman (occupation)">watermen</a> in past years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT13_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT13-6">[6]</a></sup> Recent restoration efforts begun in the 1990s have been ongoing and show potential for growth of the native oyster population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The health of the Chesapeake Bay improved in 2015, marking three years of gains over the past four years, according to a new report by the University of Maryland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>
