<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The word <i>Chesepiooc</i> is an <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_languages" title="Algonquian languages">Algonquian</a> word referring to a village "at a big river". It is the seventh oldest surviving English place-name in the U.S., first applied as "Chesepiook" by explorers heading north from the <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Colony" title="Roanoke Colony">Roanoke Colony</a> into a Chesapeake tributary in 1585 or 1586. The name may also refer to the Chesepian or Chesapeake people, a Native American tribe who inhabited the area now known as South Hampton Roads in the U.S. state of Virginia. They occupied an area which is now the Norfolk, Portsmouth, Chesapeake, and Virginia Beach areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In 2005, Algonquian linguist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blair_Rudes" title="Blair Rudes">Blair Rudes</a> "helped to dispel one of the area's most widely held beliefs: that 'Chesapeake' means something like 'great shellfish bay.' It does not, Rudes said. The name might actually have meant something like 'great water,' or it might have just referred to a village location at the bay's mouth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In addition, the name is almost always prefixed by "the" in usage by local residents: "The Chesapeake", "The Chesapeake Bay" and "The Bay".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology_and_formation">Geology and formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geology and formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Chesapeake Bay is an <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> to the North Atlantic, lying between the <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Peninsula" title="Delmarva Peninsula">Delmarva Peninsula</a> to the east and the North American mainland to the west. It is the <a href="/wiki/Ria" title="Ria">ria</a>, or drowned valley, of the <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_River" title="Susquehanna River">Susquehanna River</a>, meaning that it was the alluvial plain where the river flowed when the sea level was lower. It is not a <a href="/wiki/Fjord" title="Fjord">fjord</a>, because the <a href="/wiki/Laurentide_Ice_Sheet" title="Laurentide Ice Sheet">Laurentide Ice Sheet</a> never reached as far south as the northernmost point on the Bay. North of <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, the western shore borders the hilly <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States)" title="Piedmont (United States)">Piedmont</a> region of Maryland; south of the city the Bay lies within the state's low-lying <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_coastal_plain" title="Atlantic coastal plain">coastal plain</a>, with sedimentary cliffs to the west, and flat islands, winding creeks and marshes to the east. The large rivers entering the Bay from the west have broad mouths and are extensions of the main ria for miles up the course of each river.</p>
<p>The Bay's geology, its present form, and its very location were created by a <a href="/wiki/Bolide" title="Bolide">bolide</a> <a href="/wiki/Impact_event" title="Impact event">impact event</a> at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a> (about 35.5 million years ago), forming the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_impact_crater" title="Chesapeake Bay impact crater">Chesapeake Bay impact crater</a> and the Susquehanna River valley much later. The Bay was formed starting about 10,000 years ago when rising sea levels at the end of the last ice age flooded the Susquehanna River valley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fs102-98_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-fs102-98-4">[4]</a></sup> Parts of the Bay, especially the <a href="/wiki/Calvert_County,_Maryland" title="Calvert County, Maryland">Calvert County, Maryland</a>, coastline, are lined by cliffs composed of deposits from receding waters millions of years ago. These cliffs, generally known as <a href="/wiki/Calvert_Cliffs_State_Park" title="Calvert Cliffs State Park">Calvert Cliffs</a>, are famous for their <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">fossils</a>, especially fossilized <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">shark</a> teeth which are commonly found washed up on the beaches next to the cliffs. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientists%27_Cliffs" title="Scientists' Cliffs">Scientists' Cliffs</a> is a beach community in Calvert County named for the desire to create a retreat for scientists when the community was founded in 1935.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">Hydrology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hydrology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_-_Eastern_Bay_5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2520" data-file-width="3776" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Sunset_-_Eastern_Bay_5.jpg/220px-Sunset_-_Eastern_Bay_5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Sunset_-_Eastern_Bay_5.jpg/330px-Sunset_-_Eastern_Bay_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Sunset_-_Eastern_Bay_5.jpg/440px-Sunset_-_Eastern_Bay_5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_-_Eastern_Bay_5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of the Eastern Bay in Maryland at sunset</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis,_Maryland,_Usa_P1010854.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Annapolis%2C_Maryland%2C_Usa_P1010854.jpg/220px-Annapolis%2C_Maryland%2C_Usa_P1010854.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Annapolis%2C_Maryland%2C_Usa_P1010854.jpg/330px-Annapolis%2C_Maryland%2C_Usa_P1010854.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Annapolis%2C_Maryland%2C_Usa_P1010854.jpg/440px-Annapolis%2C_Maryland%2C_Usa_P1010854.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis,_Maryland,_Usa_P1010854.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">Chesapeake Bay Bridge</a>, near Annapolis, Maryland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Much of the Bay is shallow. At the point where the Susquehanna River flows into the Bay, the average depth is 30 feet (9 m), although this soon diminishes to an average of 10 feet (3 m) southeast of the city of <a href="/wiki/Havre_de_Grace,_Maryland" title="Havre de Grace, Maryland">Havre de Grace, Maryland</a>, to about 35 feet (11 m) just north of Annapolis. On average, the depth of the Bay is 21 feet (6.4 m), including tributaries;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> over 24 percent of the Bay is less than 6 ft (2 m) deep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chesapeake_Bay_Program:_A_Watershed_Partnership:_Facts_.26_Figures_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chesapeake_Bay_Program:_A_Watershed_Partnership:_Facts_.26_Figures-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because the Bay is an estuary, it has fresh water, salt water and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brackish" title="Brackish">brackish</a> water. Brackish water has three <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">salinity</a> zones: oligohaline, mesohaline, and <a href="/wiki/Polyhaline" title="Polyhaline">polyhaline</a>. The freshwater zone runs from the mouth of the Susquehanna River to north <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore,_Maryland" title="Baltimore, Maryland">Baltimore</a>. The oligohaline zone has very little salt. Salinity varies from 0.5 <a href="/wiki/Concentration#.22Parts-per.22_notation" title="Concentration">ppt</a> (parts per thousand) to 10 ppt, and freshwater species can survive there. The north end of the oligohaline zone is north Baltimore and the south end is the Chesapeake Bay Bridge. The mesohaline zone has a medium amount of salt and runs from the Bay Bridge to the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Rappahannock_River" title="Rappahannock River">Rappahannock River</a>. Salinity there ranges from 10.7 ppt to 18 ppt. The polyhaline zone is the saltiest zone, and some of the water can be as salty as sea water. It runs from the mouth of the Rappahannock River to the mouth of the Bay. The salinity ranges from 18.7 ppt to 36 ppt. (36 ppt is as salty as the ocean.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The climate of the area surrounding the Bay is primarily <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a>, with hot, very humid summers and cold to mild winters. Only the area around the mouth of the Susquehanna River is continental in nature, and the mouth of the Susquehanna River and the Susquehanna <a href="/wiki/Mudflat" title="Mudflat">flats</a> often freeze in winter. It is rare for the surface of the Bay to freeze in winter, something which happened most recently in the winter of 1976–77.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest rivers flowing directly into the Bay, from north to south, are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_River" title="Susquehanna River">Susquehanna River</a>:</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patapsco_River" title="Patapsco River">Patapsco River</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chester_River" title="Chester River">Chester River</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Choptank_River" title="Choptank River">Choptank River</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patuxent_River" title="Patuxent River">Patuxent River</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nanticoke_River" title="Nanticoke River">Nanticoke River</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pocomoke_River" title="Pocomoke River">Pocomoke River</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rappahannock_River" title="Rappahannock River">Rappahannock River</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/York_River_(Virginia)" title="York River (Virginia)">York River</a>;</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" title="James River (Virginia)">James River</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Another river flowing into Chesapeake Bay is the <a href="/wiki/Wicomico_River_(Maryland_eastern_shore)" title="Wicomico River (Maryland eastern shore)">Wicomico River</a>, not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Wicomico_River_(Potomac_River)" title="Wicomico River (Potomac River)">tributary of the Potomac River</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chesapeake_Waterbird_Food_Web.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="440" data-file-width="565" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Chesapeake_Waterbird_Food_Web.jpg/220px-Chesapeake_Waterbird_Food_Web.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Chesapeake_Waterbird_Food_Web.jpg/330px-Chesapeake_Waterbird_Food_Web.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Chesapeake_Waterbird_Food_Web.jpg/440px-Chesapeake_Waterbird_Food_Web.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chesapeake_Waterbird_Food_Web.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">Food chain</a> diagram for waterbirds of the Chesapeake Bay</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Chesapeake Bay is home to numerous fauna that either migrate to the Bay at some point during the year or live there year-round. There are over 300 species of <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> and numerous <a href="/wiki/Shellfish" title="Shellfish">shellfish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crab" title="Crab">crab</a> species. Some of these include the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_menhaden" title="Atlantic menhaden">Atlantic menhaden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Striped_bass" title="Striped bass">striped bass</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_eel" title="American eel">American eel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_oyster" title="Eastern oyster">eastern oyster</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Callinectes_sapidus" title="Callinectes sapidus">blue crab</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Birds include <a href="/wiki/Osprey" title="Osprey">ospreys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_blue_heron" title="Great blue heron">great blue herons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">bald eagles</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT18_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT18-19">[19]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Peregrine_falcon" title="Peregrine falcon">peregrine falcons</a>, the last two of which were threatened by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DDT" title="DDT">DDT</a>; their numbers plummeted but have risen in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESAC_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESAC-20">[20]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Piping_plover" title="Piping plover">piping plover</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near_threatened" title="Near threatened">near threatened</a> species which inhabits the wetlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESAC_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-ESAC-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Larger fish such as <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_sturgeon" title="Atlantic sturgeon">Atlantic sturgeon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> varieties of <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">sharks</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Stingray" title="Stingray">stingrays</a> visit the Chesapeake Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LifeInTheChesapeakeBay_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-LifeInTheChesapeakeBay-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title=" Dead link since December 2014">dead link</span></a></i>]</span></sup> The waters of the Chesapeake Bay have been regarded one of the most important nursery areas for sharks along east coasts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNA_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-TNA-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">Megafaunas</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Bull_shark" title="Bull shark">bull sharks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiger_shark" title="Tiger shark">tiger sharks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scalloped_hammerhead_shark" title="Scalloped hammerhead shark">scalloped hammerhead sharks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Basking_shark" title="Basking shark">basking sharks</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNA_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-TNA-25">[25]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Manta_ray" title="Manta ray">manta rays</a> are also known to visit.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">Bottlenose dolphins</a> are known to live seasonally/yearly in the Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> There have been unconfirmed sightings of <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a> in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Endangered <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_right_whale" title="North Atlantic right whale">North Atlantic right whale</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sei_whale" title="Sei whale">sei</a> whales have also been sighted within and in the vicinity of the Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LifeInTheChesapeakeBay_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-LifeInTheChesapeakeBay-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the Bay is farther north than its typical habitat range, a male <a href="/wiki/Manatee" title="Manatee">manatee</a> visited the Bay several times between 1994 and 2011. The manatee, recognizable due to distinct markings on its body, was nicknamed "Chessie" after a <a href="/wiki/Chessie_(sea_monster)" title="Chessie (sea monster)">legendary sea monster</a> that was allegedly sighted in the Bay during the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The same manatee has been spotted as far north as <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, and was the first manatee known to travel so far north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Other manatees are occasionally seen in the Bay and its tributaries, which contain sea grasses that are part of the manatee's diet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loggerhead_turtle" title="Loggerhead turtle">Loggerhead turtles</a> are known to visit the Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LifeInTheChesapeakeBay_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-LifeInTheChesapeakeBay-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Chesapeake Bay is also home to a diverse flora, both land and aquatic. Common <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Submerged_aquatic_vegetation" title="Submerged aquatic vegetation">submerged aquatic vegetation</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Zostera" title="Zostera">eelgrass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruppia_maritima" title="Ruppia maritima">widgeon grass</a>. A report in 2011 suggested that information on underwater grasses would be released, because "submerged grasses provide food and habitat for a number of species, adding oxygen to the water and improving water clarity."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT31_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT31-35">[35]</a></sup> Other vegetation that makes its home in other parts of the Bay are <a href="/wiki/Wild_rice" title="Wild rice">wild rice</a>, various trees like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_maple" title="Red maple">red maple</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bald_cypress" title="Bald cypress">bald cypress</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spartina" title="Spartina">spartina</a> grass and <a href="/wiki/Phragmites" title="Phragmites">phragmites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">Invasive plants</a> have taken a significant foothold in the Bay; plants such as <a href="/wiki/Egeria_densa" title="Egeria densa">Brazilian waterweed</a>, native to South America, have spread to most continents with the help of aquarium owners, who often dump the contents of their aquariums into nearby lakes and streams. It's highly invasive, and has the potential to flourish in the low-salinity tidal waters of the Chesapeake Bay. Dense stands of Brazilian waterweed can restrict water movement, trap sediment and affect water quality. Various local K-12 schools in the Maryland and Virginia region often have programs that cultivate native bay grasses and plant them in the Bay.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_exploration_and_settlement">European exploration and settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: European exploration and settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_map_to_label_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="314" data-file-width="450" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/First_map_to_label_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg/220px-First_map_to_label_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/First_map_to_label_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg/330px-First_map_to_label_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/First_map_to_label_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg/440px-First_map_to_label_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_map_to_label_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Revised map<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/John_White_(colonist_and_artist)" title="John White (colonist and artist)">John White's</a> original by Theodore DeBry. In this 1590 version, the Chesapeake Bay appears named for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1630_Hondius_Map_of_Virginia_and_the_Chesapeake_-_Geographicus_-_NovaVirginiaeTabula-hondius-1630.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3116" data-file-width="4000" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1630_Hondius_Map_of_Virginia_and_the_Chesapeake_-_Geographicus_-_NovaVirginiaeTabula-hondius-1630.jpg/220px-1630_Hondius_Map_of_Virginia_and_the_Chesapeake_-_Geographicus_-_NovaVirginiaeTabula-hondius-1630.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1630_Hondius_Map_of_Virginia_and_the_Chesapeake_-_Geographicus_-_NovaVirginiaeTabula-hondius-1630.jpg/330px-1630_Hondius_Map_of_Virginia_and_the_Chesapeake_-_Geographicus_-_NovaVirginiaeTabula-hondius-1630.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1630_Hondius_Map_of_Virginia_and_the_Chesapeake_-_Geographicus_-_NovaVirginiaeTabula-hondius-1630.jpg/440px-1630_Hondius_Map_of_Virginia_and_the_Chesapeake_-_Geographicus_-_NovaVirginiaeTabula-hondius-1630.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1630_Hondius_Map_of_Virginia_and_the_Chesapeake_-_Geographicus_-_NovaVirginiaeTabula-hondius-1630.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Later (1630) version of the 1612 map by Captain John Smith during his exploration of the Chesapeake. Note that the map is oriented with west at top.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1524, Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_da_Verrazzano" title="Giovanni da Verrazzano">Giovanni da Verrazzano</a>, (1485–1528), in service of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">French crown</a>, (famous for sailing through and thereafter naming the entrance to <a href="/wiki/New_York_Bay" title="New York Bay">New York Bay</a> as the "<a href="/wiki/The_Narrows" title="The Narrows">Verrazzano Narrows</a>", including now in the 20th century, a <a href="/wiki/Suspension_bridge" title="Suspension bridge">suspension bridge</a> also named for <a href="/wiki/Verrazano-Narrows_Bridge" title="Verrazano-Narrows Bridge">him</a>) sailed past the Chesapeake, but did not enter the Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parramore_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parramore-39">[39]</a></sup> Spanish explorer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucas_V%C3%A1squez_de_Ayll%C3%B3n" title="Lucas Vásquez de Ayllón">Lucas Vásquez de Ayllón</a> sent an expedition out from <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> in 1525 which reached the mouths of the Chesapeake and <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">Delaware Bays</a>. It may have been the first European expedition to explore parts of the Chesapeake Bay, which the Spaniards called "Bahía de Santa María" ("Bay of St. Mary")or "Bahía de Madre de Dios."("Bay of the Mother of God")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> De Ayllón established a short-lived <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Spain" title="Kingdom of Spain">Spanish</a> mission settlement, <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel_de_Gualdape" title="San Miguel de Gualdape">San Miguel de Gualdape</a>, in 1526 along the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic coast</a>. Many scholars doubt the assertion that it was as far north as the Chesapeake; most place it in present-day <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sapelo_Island" title="Sapelo Island">Sapelo Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In 1573, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedro_Men%C3%A9ndez_de_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Pedro Menéndez de Márquez">Pedro Menéndez de Márquez</a>, the governor of Spanish Florida, conducted further exploration of the Chesapeake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parramore_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Parramore-39">[39]</a></sup> In 1570, Spanish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">Jesuits</a> established the short-lived <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ajacan_Mission" title="Ajacan Mission">Ajacan Mission</a> on one of the Chesapeake tributaries in present-day Virginia.</p>
<p>The arrival of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a> colonists under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Walter_Raleigh" title="Sir Walter Raleigh">Sir Walter Raleigh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Gilbert" title="Humphrey Gilbert">Humphrey Gilbert</a> in the late 16th century to found a colony, later settled at <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Island" title="Roanoke Island">Roanoke Island</a> (off the present-day coast of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>) for the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Company" title="Virginia Company">Virginia Company</a>, marked the first time that the English approached the gates to Chesapeake Bay between the capes of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Charles_(headland)" title="Cape Charles (headland)">Cape Charles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Henry" title="Cape Henry">Cape Henry</a>. Three decades later, in 1607, Europeans again entered the Bay. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_John_Smith" title="Captain John Smith">Captain John Smith</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> explored and mapped the Bay between 1607 and 1609, resulting in the publication in 1612 back in the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> of <i>"A Map of Virginia"</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SmithMapinfo_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-SmithMapinfo-42">[42]</a></sup> Smith wrote in his journal: "Heaven and earth have never agreed better to frame a place for man's habitation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT21_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT21-43">[43]</a></sup> The new laying out of the "<a href="/wiki/Captain_John_Smith_Chesapeake_National_Historic_Trail" title="Captain John Smith Chesapeake National Historic Trail">Captain John Smith Chesapeake National Historic Trail</a>", the United States' first designated "all-water" <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Trail" title="National Historic Trail">National Historic Trail</a>, was created in July 2006, by the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">U.S. Department of the Interior</a> following the route of Smith's historic 17th-century voyage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Because of economic hardships and civil strife in the "Mother Land", there was a mass migration of southern English <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">Cavaliers</a> and their servants to the Chesapeake Bay region between 1640 and 1675, to both of the new colonies of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Virginia" title="Province of Virginia">Province of Virginia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maryland" title="Province of Maryland">Province of Maryland</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Revolution_to_the_present">American Revolution to the present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: American Revolution to the present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Chesapeake Bay was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Chesapeake" title="Battle of the Chesapeake">Battle of the Chesapeake</a> (also known as the "Battle of the Capes", <a href="/wiki/Cape_Charles_(headland)" title="Cape Charles (headland)">Cape Charles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Henry" title="Cape Henry">Cape Henry</a>) in 1781, during which the French fleet defeated the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> in the decisive naval battle of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>. The British defeat enabled <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">General George Washington</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">French</a> allied armies under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Donatien_de_Vimeur,_Comte_de_Rochambeau" title="Jean-Baptiste Donatien de Vimeur, Comte de Rochambeau">Comte de Rochambeau</a> to march down from <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_City" title="History of New York City">New York</a> and bottle up the rampaging southern <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Cornwallis" title="Lord Cornwallis">Lord Cornwallis</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_in_the_American_Revolution" title="North Carolina in the American Revolution">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_in_the_American_Revolution" title="South Carolina in the American Revolution">South</a> Carolinas at the siege of <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Battle of Yorktown</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">Yorktown, Virginia</a>. Their marching route from <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport, Rhode Island</a> through Connecticut, New York State, Pennsylvania, New Jersey and Delaware to the <a href="/wiki/Elkton,_Maryland" title="Elkton, Maryland">"Head of Elk"</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_River" title="Susquehanna River">Susquehanna River</a> along the shores and also partially sailing down the Bay to <a href="/wiki/History_of_Virginia" title="History of Virginia">Virginia</a>. It is also the subject of a designated <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Trail" title="National Historic Trail">National Historic Trail</a> under the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington-Rochambeau_Revolutionary_Route" title="Washington-Rochambeau Revolutionary Route">Washington-Rochambeau Revolutionary Route</a>.</p>
<p>The Bay would again see conflict during <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>. During the year of 1813, from their base on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangier_Island" title="Tangier Island">Tangier Island</a>, British naval forces under the command of Admiral <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Cockburn" title="George Cockburn">George Cockburn</a> raided and plundered several towns on the shores of the Chesapeake, treating the Bay as if it were a "British Lake". The <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Flotilla" title="Chesapeake Bay Flotilla">Chesapeake Bay Flotilla</a>, a fleet of shallow-draft armed barges under the command of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">U.S. Navy</a> Commodore <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Barney" title="Joshua Barney">Joshua Barney</a>, was assembled to stall British shore raids and attacks. After months of harassment by Barney, the British landed on the west side of the Patuxent at <a href="/wiki/Benedict,_Maryland" title="Benedict, Maryland">Benedict, Maryland</a>, the Chesapeake Flotilla was scuttled, and the British trekked overland to <a href="/wiki/Burning_of_Washington" title="Burning of Washington">burn the US Capitol</a> in August 1814. A few days later in a "pincer attack", they also sailed up the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a> to attack <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Washington_(Maryland)" title="Fort Washington (Maryland)">Fort Washington</a> below the National Capital and demanded a ransom from the nearby port town of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Virginia" title="Alexandria, Virginia">Alexandria, Virginia</a>.</p>
<p>There were so-called "<a href="/wiki/Oyster_Wars" title="Oyster Wars">Oyster Wars</a>" in the late 19th and early 20th centuries. Until the mid-20th century, oyster harvesting rivaled the crab industry among Chesapeake watermen, a dwindling breed whose <a href="/wiki/Skipjack_(boat)" title="Skipjack (boat)">skipjacks</a> and other workboats were supplanted by recreational craft in the latter part of the century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT22_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT22-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1960s, the <a href="/wiki/Calvert_Cliffs_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Calvert Cliffs Nuclear Power Plant">Calvert Cliffs Nuclear Power Plant</a> on the historic <a href="/wiki/Calvert_Cliffs_State_Park" title="Calvert Cliffs State Park">Calvert Cliffs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calvert_County,_Maryland" title="Calvert County, Maryland">Calvert County</a> on the Western Shore of Maryland began using water from the Bay to cool its reactor.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Navigation">Navigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Navigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ltshp.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ltshp.JPG/220px-Ltshp.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ltshp.JPG/330px-Ltshp.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ltshp.JPG/440px-Ltshp.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ltshp.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lighthouses and <a href="/wiki/Lightvessel" title="Lightvessel">lightships</a> such as <a href="/wiki/United_States_lightship_Chesapeake_(LV-116)" title="United States lightship Chesapeake (LV-116)"><i>Chesapeake</i></a> have helped guide ships into the Bay</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Chesapeake Bay forms a link in the <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway" title="Intracoastal Waterway">Intracoastal Waterway</a>, of the bays, sounds and inlets between the off-shore barrier islands and the coastal mainland along the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic coast</a> connecting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Delaware_Canal" title="Chesapeake and Delaware Canal">Chesapeake and Delaware Canal</a> (linking the Bay to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a>) with the <a href="/wiki/Albemarle_and_Chesapeake_Canal" title="Albemarle and Chesapeake Canal">Albemarle and Chesapeake Canal</a> (linking the Bay, to the south, via the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_River_(Virginia)" title="Elizabeth River (Virginia)">Elizabeth River</a>, by the cities of <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">Portsmouth</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Albemarle_Sound" title="Albemarle Sound">Albemarle Sound</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pamlico_Sound" title="Pamlico Sound">Pamlico Sound</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> and further to the Sea Islands of Georgia). A busy shipping channel (dredged by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">U.S. Army Corps of Engineers</a> since the 1850s) runs the length of the Bay, is an important transit route for large vessels entering or leaving the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helen_Delich_Bentley_Port_of_Baltimore" title="Helen Delich Bentley Port of Baltimore">Port of Baltimore</a>, and further north through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Delaware_Canal" title="Chesapeake and Delaware Canal">Chesapeake and Delaware Canal</a> to the ports of <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">Wilmington</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a>.</p>
<p>During the later half of the 19th century and first half of the 20th century, the Bay was plied by passenger steamships and packet boat lines connecting the various cities on it, notably the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Steam_Packet_Company" title="Baltimore Steam Packet Company">Baltimore Steam Packet Company</a> ("Old Bay Line").</p>
<p>In the later 20th century, a series of road crossings were built. One, the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">Chesapeake Bay Bridge</a> (also known as the Governor William Preston Lane, Jr. Memorial Bridge) between the state capital of <a href="/wiki/Annapolis,_Maryland" title="Annapolis, Maryland">Annapolis, Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matapeake,_Maryland" title="Matapeake, Maryland">Matapeake</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">Eastern Shore</a>, crossing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kent_Island,_Maryland" title="Kent Island, Maryland">Kent Island</a>, was constructed 1949-1952. A second, parallel, span was added in 1973. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge-Tunnel" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel">Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel</a>, connecting <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Virginia" title="Eastern Shore of Virginia">Virginia's Eastern Shore</a> with its mainland (at the metropolitan areas of <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">Portsmouth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">Chesapeake</a>), is approximately 20 miles (32 km) long; it has trestle bridges as well as two stretches of two-mile-long (3.2 km) tunnels which allow unimpeded shipping; the bridge is supported by four 5.25-acre (21,200 m<sup>2</sup>) man-made islands. The Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel was opened for two lanes in 1964 and four lanes in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT25_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT25-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tides">Tides</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tides">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tide_final4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="804" data-file-width="361" height="490" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Tide_final4.jpg/220px-Tide_final4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Tide_final4.jpg/330px-Tide_final4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/09/Tide_final4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tide_final4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Example Chesapeake Bay tides from Baltimore and the Chesapeake Bay Bridge Tunnel for quarter and full moons during June 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">Tides</a> in the Chesapeake Bay exhibit an interesting and unique behavior due to the nature of the topography (both horizontal and vertical shape), wind driven circulation, and how the Bay interacts with oceanic tides. Research into the peculiar behavior of tides both at the northern and southern extents of the Bay began in the late 1970s. One study noted sea level fluctuations at periods of 5 days, driven by sea level changes at the Bay’s mouth on the Atlantic coast and local lateral winds, and 2.5 days, caused by resonant oscillations driven by local longitudinal winds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> while another study later found that the geometry of the Bay permits for a resonant period of 1.46 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>A good example of how the different Chesapeake Bay sites experience different tides can be seen in the tidal predictions published by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Oceanographic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanographic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanographic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (NOAA) (see figure at right).</p>
<p>At the Chesapeake Bay Bridge Tunnel (CBBT) site, which lies at the southernmost point of the Bay where it meets the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> near <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk, Virginia</a> and the capes of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Charles_(headland)" title="Cape Charles (headland)">Charles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Henry" title="Cape Henry">Henry</a>, there is a distinct semi-diurnal tide throughout the lunar month, with small amplitude modulations during spring (new/full moon) vs. neap (one/three quarter moon) tidal periods. The main forcing of the CBBT tides are typical, semi-diurnal ocean tides that the East Coast of the United States experiences.</p>
<p>Baltimore, in the northern portion of the Bay, experiences a noticeable modulation to form its mixed tidal nature during spring vs. neap tides. Spring tides, when the sun-earth-moon system forms a line, cause the largest tidal amplitudes during lunar monthly tidal variations. In contrast, neap tides, when the sun-earth-moon system forms a right angle, are muted, and in a semi-diurnal tidal system (such as that seen at the CBBT site) this can be seen as a lowest intertidal range.</p>
<p>Two interesting points that arise from comparing these two sites at opposite ends of the Bay are their tidal characteristics - semi-diurnal tide for CBBT and mixed tide for Baltimore (due to resonance in the Bay) - and the differences in amplitude (due to dissipation in the Bay).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing_industry">Fishing industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fishing industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skipjack_EPA.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="234" data-file-width="289" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Skipjack_EPA.PNG/220px-Skipjack_EPA.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/de/Skipjack_EPA.PNG 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skipjack_EPA.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Skipjack_(boat)" title="Skipjack (boat)">skipjack</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Oyster#Fishing_from_the_wild" title="Oyster">oystering</a> fleet in Maryland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Bay is mostly known for its seafood production, especially blue crabs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT19_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT19-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Clam" title="Clam">clams</a> and oysters. In the middle of the 20th century, the Bay supported 9,000 full-time watermen, according to one account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT19_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsT19-50">[50]</a></sup> Today, the body of water is less productive than it used to be because of <a href="/wiki/Surface_runoff" title="Surface runoff">runoff</a> from <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a> (mostly on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Shore" title="Western Shore">Western Shore</a>) and farms (especially on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maryland_Eastern_Shore" title="Maryland Eastern Shore">Eastern Shore</a> and in the Susquehanna River watershed), over-harvesting, and <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasion of foreign species</a>.</p>
<p>The plentiful oyster harvests led to the development of the <a href="/wiki/Skipjack_(boat)" title="Skipjack (boat)">skipjack</a>, the state boat of Maryland, which is the only remaining working boat type in the United States still under sail power. Other characteristic Bay-area workboats include sail-powered boats such as the <a href="/wiki/Log_canoe" title="Log canoe">log canoe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pungy" title="Pungy">pungy</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bugeye_(boat)" title="Bugeye (boat)">bugeye</a>, and the motorized <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_deadrise" title="Chesapeake Bay deadrise">Chesapeake Bay deadrise</a>, the state boat of Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>In contrast to harvesting wild oysters, <a href="/wiki/Oyster_farming" title="Oyster farming">oyster farming</a> is a growing industry for the Bay to help maintain the estuary's productivity as well as a natural effort for filtering impurities such as <a href="/wiki/Nutrient_pollution" title="Nutrient pollution">excess nutrients</a> from the water in an effort to reduce the effects of man-made <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">pollution</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Program" title="Chesapeake Bay Program">Chesapeake Bay Program</a> is using oysters to reduce the amount of nitrogen compounds entering the Chesapeake Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Oysters are hermaphroditic and will change gender at least once during their lifetime, often starting as male and ending as female; there are numerous ways to cook and eat them, as well as recipes and sauces to accompany oyster dishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT22_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsT22-45">[45]</a></sup> One account:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The Chesapeake oyster – sometimes called Chesapeake white gold – has a flavor and texture that begs connoisseurs to come back and shuck just a few more.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Kendra Bailey Morris, <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a>, 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT22_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-twsT22-45">[45]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>The Bay is famous for its rockfish, a regional name for <a href="/wiki/Striped_bass" title="Striped bass">striped bass</a>. Once on the verge of extinction, rockfish have made a significant comeback because of legislative action that put a moratorium on rockfishing, which allowed the species to re-populate. Rockfish can now be fished in strictly controlled and limited quantities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_and_recreation">Tourism and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tourism and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Point_Lighthouse_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="978" data-file-width="1245" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Thomas_Point_Lighthouse_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg/220px-Thomas_Point_Lighthouse_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Thomas_Point_Lighthouse_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg/330px-Thomas_Point_Lighthouse_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Thomas_Point_Lighthouse_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg/440px-Thomas_Point_Lighthouse_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Point_Lighthouse_Chesapeake_Bay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Point_Shoal_Light" title="Thomas Point Shoal Light">Thomas Point Shoal Light</a> in Maryland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Chesapeake Bay is a main feature for tourists who visit Maryland and Virginia each year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Fishing, crabbing, swimming, boating, kayaking,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT18_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsT18-19">[19]</a></sup> and sailing are extremely popular activities enjoyed on the waters of the Chesapeake Bay. As a result, tourism has a notable impact on Maryland's economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> One report suggested that Annapolis was an appealing spot for families, water sports and boating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT24_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT24-54">[54]</a></sup> Commentator Terry Smith spoke about the Bay's beauty:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The water is glassy, smooth and gorgeous, his wake white against the deep blue. That's the problem with the Chesapeake. It's so damned beautiful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT21_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsT21-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>One account suggested how the Chesapeake attracts people:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>You see them everywhere on Maryland's Eastern Shore, the weekend sailors. They are unmistakable with their deep tans, their baggy shorts, their frayed polo shirts, their Top-Siders worn without socks. Some may not even own their own boats, much less win regattas, but they are inexorably drawn to the Chesapeake Bay ... I planned to spend my days boating, eating as many Chesapeake Bay blue crabs as possible and making a little study of Eastern Shore locals. For city folk like me, they're interesting, even exotic –the weather-beaten crabbers and oystermen called "watermen," gentlemen-farmers and sharecroppers, boat builders, antiques dealers – all of whom sound like Southerners with mouthfuls of marbles when they talk. — Susan Spano, <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, 2008<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT27_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT27-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_problems">Environmental problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Environmental problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution_and_runoff">Pollution and runoff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Pollution and runoff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Program" title="Chesapeake Bay Program">Chesapeake Bay Program</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ChesapeakeTidalWetlands.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/ChesapeakeTidalWetlands.jpg/220px-ChesapeakeTidalWetlands.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/ChesapeakeTidalWetlands.jpg/330px-ChesapeakeTidalWetlands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/ChesapeakeTidalWetlands.jpg/440px-ChesapeakeTidalWetlands.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ChesapeakeTidalWetlands.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tidal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wetlands" title="Wetlands">wetlands</a> of the Chesapeake Bay</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DEAD_MENHADEN_FLOAT_ALONG_THE_TIDE_LINE_JUST_NORTH_OF_THE_CHESAPEAKE_BAY_BRIDGE_-_NARA_-_546836.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2011" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/DEAD_MENHADEN_FLOAT_ALONG_THE_TIDE_LINE_JUST_NORTH_OF_THE_CHESAPEAKE_BAY_BRIDGE_-_NARA_-_546836.jpg/170px-DEAD_MENHADEN_FLOAT_ALONG_THE_TIDE_LINE_JUST_NORTH_OF_THE_CHESAPEAKE_BAY_BRIDGE_-_NARA_-_546836.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/DEAD_MENHADEN_FLOAT_ALONG_THE_TIDE_LINE_JUST_NORTH_OF_THE_CHESAPEAKE_BAY_BRIDGE_-_NARA_-_546836.jpg/255px-DEAD_MENHADEN_FLOAT_ALONG_THE_TIDE_LINE_JUST_NORTH_OF_THE_CHESAPEAKE_BAY_BRIDGE_-_NARA_-_546836.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/DEAD_MENHADEN_FLOAT_ALONG_THE_TIDE_LINE_JUST_NORTH_OF_THE_CHESAPEAKE_BAY_BRIDGE_-_NARA_-_546836.jpg/340px-DEAD_MENHADEN_FLOAT_ALONG_THE_TIDE_LINE_JUST_NORTH_OF_THE_CHESAPEAKE_BAY_BRIDGE_-_NARA_-_546836.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DEAD_MENHADEN_FLOAT_ALONG_THE_TIDE_LINE_JUST_NORTH_OF_THE_CHESAPEAKE_BAY_BRIDGE_-_NARA_-_546836.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Environmental Protection Agency photo of dead menhaden floating in the Bay in June 1973</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HPIM0077.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1312" data-file-width="1792" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/HPIM0077.JPG/220px-HPIM0077.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/HPIM0077.JPG/330px-HPIM0077.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/HPIM0077.JPG/440px-HPIM0077.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HPIM0077.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Reeds along the Bay</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1970s, the Chesapeake Bay was found to contain one of the planet's first identified <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_dead_zone" title="Marine dead zone">marine dead zones</a>, where waters were so depleted of oxygen that they were unable to support life, resulting in massive <a href="/wiki/Fish_kill" title="Fish kill">fish kills</a>. Today the Bay's dead zones are estimated to kill 75,000 tons of bottom-dwelling clams and worms each year, weakening the base of the estuary's <a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">food chain</a> and robbing the blue crab in particular of a primary food source. Crabs are sometimes observed to amass on shore to escape pockets of oxygen-poor water, a behavior known as a "crab jubilee". <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(environmental)" title="Hypoxia (environmental)">Hypoxia</a> results in part from large <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">algal blooms</a>, which are nourished by the runoff of residential, farm and industrial <a href="/wiki/Wastewater" title="Wastewater">waste</a> throughout the watershed. One report in 2010 criticized <a href="/wiki/Amish" title="Amish">Amish</a> farmers for having cows which "generate heaps of manure that easily washes into streams and flows onward into the Chesapeake Bay".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT23_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT23-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_080608-N-2568S-023_Sailors_assigned_to_the_amphibious_assault_ship_USS_Wasp_(LHD_1)_look_for_trash_on_the_shore_of_the_Chesapeake_Bay_during_Clean_The_Bay_Day.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/US_Navy_080608-N-2568S-023_Sailors_assigned_to_the_amphibious_assault_ship_USS_Wasp_%28LHD_1%29_look_for_trash_on_the_shore_of_the_Chesapeake_Bay_during_Clean_The_Bay_Day.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/US_Navy_080608-N-2568S-023_Sailors_assigned_to_the_amphibious_assault_ship_USS_Wasp_%28LHD_1%29_look_for_trash_on_the_shore_of_the_Chesapeake_Bay_during_Clean_The_Bay_Day.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/US_Navy_080608-N-2568S-023_Sailors_assigned_to_the_amphibious_assault_ship_USS_Wasp_%28LHD_1%29_look_for_trash_on_the_shore_of_the_Chesapeake_Bay_during_Clean_The_Bay_Day.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_080608-N-2568S-023_Sailors_assigned_to_the_amphibious_assault_ship_USS_Wasp_(LHD_1)_look_for_trash_on_the_shore_of_the_Chesapeake_Bay_during_Clean_The_Bay_Day.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. Navy sailors looking for trash during "Clean The Bay Day" in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The runoff and pollution have many components that help contribute to the algal bloom, which is mainly fed by <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">phosphorus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> This algae prevents sunlight from reaching the bottom of the Bay while alive and deoxygenates the Bay's water when it dies and rots. The erosion and runoff of <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sediment</a> into the Bay, exacerbated by devegetation, construction and the prevalence of pavement in urban and suburban areas, also blocks vital sunlight. The resulting loss of <a href="/wiki/Aquatic_plant" title="Aquatic plant">aquatic vegetation</a> has depleted the habitat for much of the Bay's animal life. Beds of <a href="/wiki/Zostera" title="Zostera">eelgrass</a>, the dominant variety in the southern Bay, have shrunk by more than half there since the early 1970s. Overharvesting, pollution, sedimentation and disease have turned much of the Bay's bottom into a muddy wasteland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>One particularly harmful source of <a href="/wiki/Toxicity" title="Toxicity">toxicity</a> is <i><a href="/wiki/Pfiesteria_piscicida" title="Pfiesteria piscicida">Pfiesteria piscicida</a></i>, which can affect both fish and humans. <i>Pfiesteria</i> caused a small regional panic in the late 1990s when a series of large blooms started killing large numbers of fish while giving swimmers mysterious rashes; nutrient runoff from chicken farms was blamed for the growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bay improved slightly in terms of the overall health of its ecosystem, earning a rating of 31 out of 100 in 2010, up from 28 in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT16_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-twsT16-2">[2]</a></sup> An estimate in 2006 from a "blue ribbon panel" said cleanup costs would be $15 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT21_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-twsT21-43">[43]</a></sup> Compounding the problem is that 100,000 new residents move to the area each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT21_43-3"><a href="#cite_note-twsT21-43">[43]</a></sup> A report in 2008 in the <i>Washington Post</i> suggested that government administrators had overstated progress on cleanup efforts as a way to "preserve the flow of federal and state money to the project."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT12_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT12-60">[60]</a></sup> In January 2011, there were reports that millions of fish had died, but officials suggested it was probably the result of extremely cold weather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT11_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT11-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Depletion_of_oysters">Depletion of oysters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Depletion of oysters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oyster_wars_1886_Harpers_Weekly.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="2167" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Oyster_wars_1886_Harpers_Weekly.jpeg/220px-Oyster_wars_1886_Harpers_Weekly.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Oyster_wars_1886_Harpers_Weekly.jpeg/330px-Oyster_wars_1886_Harpers_Weekly.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Oyster_wars_1886_Harpers_Weekly.jpeg/440px-Oyster_wars_1886_Harpers_Weekly.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oyster_wars_1886_Harpers_Weekly.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Oyster_Wars" title="Oyster Wars">Oyster boats at war</a> off the Maryland shore (1886 wood engraving). Regulation of the oyster beds in Virginia and Maryland has existed since the 19th century.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While the Bay's salinity is ideal for oysters and the oyster fishery was at one time the Bay's most commercially viable,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-econ_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-econ-62">[62]</a></sup> the population has in the last fifty years been devastated. Maryland once had roughly 200,000 acres (810 km<sup>2</sup>) of oyster reefs. Today it has about 36,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-econ_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-econ-62">[62]</a></sup> It has been estimated that in pre-colonial times, oysters could filter the entirety of the Bay in about 3.3 days; by 1988 this time had increased to 325 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The harvest's gross value decreased 88% from 1982 to 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> One report suggested the Bay had fewer oysters in 2008 than 25 years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT13_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsT13-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Corps_of_Engineers_restoring_oysters_in_Chesapeake_tributaries.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="683" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Corps_of_Engineers_restoring_oysters_in_Chesapeake_tributaries.jpg/170px-Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Corps_of_Engineers_restoring_oysters_in_Chesapeake_tributaries.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Corps_of_Engineers_restoring_oysters_in_Chesapeake_tributaries.jpg/255px-Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Corps_of_Engineers_restoring_oysters_in_Chesapeake_tributaries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Corps_of_Engineers_restoring_oysters_in_Chesapeake_tributaries.jpg/340px-Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Corps_of_Engineers_restoring_oysters_in_Chesapeake_tributaries.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_The_U.S._Army_-_Corps_of_Engineers_restoring_oysters_in_Chesapeake_tributaries.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A cluster of oysters grown in a sanctuary</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The primary problem is overharvesting. Lax government regulations allow anyone with a license to remove oysters from state-owned beds, and although limits are set, they are not strongly enforced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-econ_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-econ-62">[62]</a></sup> The overharvesting of oysters has made it difficult for them to reproduce, which requires close proximity to one another. A second cause for the oyster depletion is that the drastic increase in human population caused a sharp increase in pollution flowing into the Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-econ_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-econ-62">[62]</a></sup> The Bay's oyster industry has also suffered from two diseases: <a href="/wiki/Haplosporidium_nelsoni" title="Haplosporidium nelsoni">MSX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Perkinsus_marinus" title="Perkinsus marinus">Dermo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>The depletion of oysters has had a particularly harmful effect on the quality of the Bay. Oysters serve as natural water filters, and their decline has further reduced the water quality of the Bay. Water that was once clear for meters is now so <a href="/wiki/Turbidity" title="Turbidity">turbid</a> that a wader may lose sight of his feet while his knees are still dry.</p>
<p>Efforts of federal, state and local governments, working in partnership through the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Program" title="Chesapeake Bay Program">Chesapeake Bay Program</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Foundation" title="Chesapeake Bay Foundation">Chesapeake Bay Foundation</a> and other nonprofit environmental groups, to restore or at least maintain the current <a href="/wiki/Water_quality" title="Water quality">water quality</a> have had mixed results. One particular obstacle to cleaning up the Bay is that much of the polluting substances arise far upstream in <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a> lying within states far removed from the Bay. Despite the state of Maryland spending over $100 million to restore the Bay, conditions have continued to grow worse. Twenty years ago, the Bay supported over six thousand oystermen. There are now fewer than 500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Efforts to repopulate the Bay via hatcheries have been carried out by a group called the Oyster Recovery Partnership, with some success. They recently placed 6 million oysters on eight acres (32,000 m<sup>2</sup>) of the Trent Hall sanctuary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-som_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-som-67">[67]</a></sup> Scientists from the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Institute_of_Marine_Science" title="Virginia Institute of Marine Science">Virginia Institute of Marine Science</a> at the <a href="/wiki/College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="College of William &amp; Mary">College of William &amp; Mary</a> claim that experimental reefs created in 2004 now house 180 million native oysters, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crassostrea_virginica" title="Crassostrea virginica">Crassostrea virginica</a></i>, which is far fewer than the billions that once existed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Times-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">Publications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Publications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are several magazines and publications that cover topics directly related to the Chesapeake Bay and life and tourism within the Bay region.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Capital" title="The Capital">The Capital</a></i>, a newspaper based in Annapolis, reports about news pertaining to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Western Shore of Maryland">Western Shore of Maryland</a> and the Annapolis area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACN_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACN-69">[69]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Magazine" title="Chesapeake Bay Magazine">Chesapeake Bay Magazine</a></i> and <i><a class="external text" href="http://www.proptalk.com/" rel="nofollow">PropTalk</a></i> focus on powerboating, while <i><a class="external text" href="http://www.spinsheet.com/" rel="nofollow">SpinSheet</a></i> focuses on sailing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBB_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBB-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-proptalk_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-proptalk-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spinsheet_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-spinsheet-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_depictions">Cultural depictions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cultural depictions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_literature">In literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: In literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beautiful_Swimmers:_Watermen,_Crabs_and_the_Chesapeake_Bay" title="Beautiful Swimmers: Watermen, Crabs and the Chesapeake Bay">Beautiful Swimmers: Watermen, Crabs and the Chesapeake Bay</a></i> (1976) is a <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>-winning non-fiction book by <a href="/wiki/William_W._Warner" title="William W. Warner">William W. Warner</a> about the Chesapeake Bay, blue crabs and watermen.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_(novel)" title="Chesapeake (novel)">Chesapeake</a></i>, a 1978 novel by author <a href="/wiki/James_A._Michener" title="James A. Michener">James A. Michener</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Barth" title="John Barth">John Barth</a> wrote two novels featuring Chesapeake Bay; <i><a href="/wiki/Sabbatical:_A_Romance" title="Sabbatical: A Romance">Sabbatical: A Romance</a></i> (1982) centered on a yacht race through the Bay, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tidewater_Tales" title="The Tidewater Tales">The Tidewater Tales</a></i> (1987) detailed a married couple telling stories to each other as they cruise the Bay.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Jacob_Have_I_Loved" title="Jacob Have I Loved">Jacob Have I Loved</a></i> (1980) by <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Paterson" title="Katherine Paterson">Katherine Paterson</a>, winner of the 1981 <a href="/wiki/Newbery_Medal" title="Newbery Medal">Newbery Medal</a>. This is a novel about the relationship between two sisters in a waterman family who grow up on an island in the Bay.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Tom_Clancy" title="Tom Clancy">Tom Clancy</a>'s 1987 book <i><a href="/wiki/Patriot_Games" title="Patriot Games">Patriot Games</a></i>, the main protagonist Jack Ryan lives on the fictional Peregrine Cliffs which overlook the Chesapeake Bay.</li>
<li>Class conflict between waterman people and wealthy newcomers was portrayed in Priscilla Cummings's novel <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Kayak" title="Red Kayak">Red Kayak</a></i>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_film">In film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: In film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Bay_(film)" title="The Bay (film)">The Bay</a></i>, a 2012 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Found_footage_(pseudo-documentary)" title="Found footage (pseudo-documentary)">found footage</a>-style eco-horror movie about a <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemic</a> due to deadly pollution from chicken factory farm run-off and mutant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isopods" title="Isopods">isopods</a> and aquatic parasites able to infect humans.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_media">Other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chesapeake_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Singer and songwriter Tom Wisner recorded several albums, often about the Chesapeake Bay. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> wrote that Wisner "always tried to capture the voice of the water and the sky, of the rocks and the trees, of the fish and the birds, of the gods of nature he believed still watched over it all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT32_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsT32-73">[73]</a></sup> He was known as the <i>Bard of the Chesapeake Bay.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsT32_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsT32-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 1976 hit "<a href="/wiki/Moonlight_Feels_Right" title="Moonlight Feels Right">Moonlight Feels Right</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Starbuck_(band)" title="Starbuck (band)">Starbuck</a> refers to Chesapeake Bay: "I'll take you on a trip beside the ocean / And drop the top at Chesapeake Bay."</p>

<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Also shown as "Chisupioc" (by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Smith_of_Jamestown" title="John Smith of Jamestown">John Smith</a>) and "Chisapeack", in Algonquian "che" means "big" or "great", "sepi" means river, and the "oc" or "ok" ending indicated something (a village, in this case) "at" that feature. "Sepi" is also found in another placename of <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_languages" title="Algonquian languages">Algonquian</a> origin, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi</a>. The name was soon transferred by the English from the big river and the village at that site to the entire bay. <cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/George_R._Stewart" title="George R. Stewart">Stewart, George</a> (1945). <i>Names on the Land: A Historical Account of Place-Naming in the United States</i>. New York: Random House. p. 23.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChesapeake+Bay&amp;rft.aufirst=George&amp;rft.aulast=Stewart&amp;rft.btitle=Names+on+the+Land%3A+A+Historical+Account+of+Place-Naming+in+the+United+States&amp;rft.date=1945&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=23&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Random+House&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
